Li Fengxiang Tragically Commits Suicide After Communist Bandits Abduct His Wife and Murder His Son

＝His Elderly Father Barely Escapes with His Life, a Single Letter Tears Him Apart＝

He Locks Himself in a Hotel Room, Ingests Opium, and Dies

Yesterday morning at about 1 AM, a man suddenly checked into the Hongyun Hotel at No. 1009 Haining Road. He claimed to be Li Fengxiang, a native of Jiangxi, 31 years old, and a bookkeeper at the Jiankang Association in this port. The hotel assigned him Room 112. Li paid one yuan for the room and went to sleep. Unexpectedly, at about 2 AM, the night watchman suddenly heard moaning from the room, suspecting that he had suddenly contracted an epidemic. He hurriedly tried to open the door and enter, and saw Li Fengxiang's face was pale. He was tossing and turning in bed, calling out in pain. When asked if he was sick, he shook his head and said nothing. After repeated questioning by the bookkeeper, he finally said that he had ingested poison. The hotel immediately reported to the Hongkou police station, who sent Li to Tongren Hospital for treatment. After the hospital examined him, they discovered that he had ingested a large amount of raw opium, which had already saturated his blood. He ultimately died despite efforts to save him. The hospital reported the death to the police station, who transferred the body to the autopsy institute. At the same time, the police found a letter from his father in Jiangxi on the deceased. The letter stated that the Communist bandits were rampant in his hometown of Jiangxi. Fengxiang's wife had been abducted by the Communist bandits, and his son had been brutally murdered. Only Li's elderly father had escaped, and he was now alone, penniless, and unable to escape the clutches of the bandits. The situation was tragic and heartbreaking. Therefore, it is speculated that Li's suicide was indirectly caused by the Communist bandits. How tragic!

Gu Naijuan Sues Her Father to Confirm Her Paternity

Her Biological Mother Has Divorced Her Father

Testified in Court Yesterday on Behalf of Her Daughter

Gu Pinjian, the owner of Zhengtai Cotton Yarn Shop at No. 740 Yongkang Lane, Beijing Road, is nearly fifty years old and originally from Jiading. On September 19, 1913, he married a woman surnamed Lu. On October 26 of the following year, they had a daughter named Naijuan. They lived together harmoniously for more than ten years. However, in 1924, Gu Pinjian and Gu Lu divorced due to differing opinions. At that time, Gu Naijuan was only twelve years old. It was stated that Gu Naijuan would be temporarily taken by her biological mother for care. Gu Pinjian then remarried. Because he had no children with his second wife, he adopted two sons, one now ten years old and the other only seven. Now that Gu Naijuan has reached the age of twenty, she has gradually gained knowledge. Because drifting outside for so long is not a good plan, she asked to return home to live last April. Unexpectedly, Gu Pinjian not only refused her request but also denied that she was his daughter. After Naijuan repeatedly pleaded, her stepmother suggested that Naijuan be fostered at the home of Gu Pinjian's friend, Wang Baosheng. But even in June of this year, they were still separated and unable to live at home. Helplessly, she hired lawyers Jiang Chipin and Qiu Fenling to petition the First Special District Court for mediation. Because Gu Pinjian did not attend, it was not established. She then filed a lawsuit asking the court to legally determine that Gu Pinjian was her biological father and allow her to return home, so that they could be reunited. The court approved the request and held a hearing on June 9. The defendant, Gu Pinjian, also hired lawyer Ye Fukan to defend him. Because witnesses needed to be added, the hearing was rescheduled for yesterday morning. Yesterday morning at 9:30 AM, Judge Luo opened the 14th Civil Court for questioning. First, Gu Naijuan testified, "I went to my uncle's place on September 20, 1931, and in April 1932, my uncle sent me back to my mother's house. I went to my father's place again on April 26 of last year, and then my father sent me to the home of his friend Wang Baosheng to be fostered." Next, the witness Pu Zhijun (Naijuan's uncle) testified, "In September 1913, Gu Pinjian married a woman surnamed Lu. In October 1914, they had Naijuan. I was invited to the full-month celebration. In September 1931, Naijuan came to my house and asked me to discuss with her father Gu Pinjian to let her return home. I discussed it with Gu, and Gu said that she would be temporarily fostered in my house. However, Gu said at the time that it would be for three months, and then Gu would take her back. But after the three months were up, I repeatedly urged him to take her back, but Gu repeatedly postponed it. I had no choice but to send Naijuan to her biological mother's place last April, intending for Naijuan to discuss it with her biological mother first before deciding on a solution." Finally, Gu Lu testified, "I married Gu Pinjian on September 19, 1913, and had Naijuan on October 26, 1914. In 1924, Gu Pinjian and I had disagreements and divorced. However, because Naijuan was still young at the time, she was temporarily cared for by me." Judge Luo postponed the hearing to the morning of the 19th of this month to add Pu Zhijun's brother to the case for questioning. Then, the court adjourned.

Smuggled Artificial Silk of Ningbo Material Confiscated

＝Bound for Hankou and Tianjin＝

Will Also Be Returned to Shanghai Within Days

The Wanguo Express Warehouse Company in this port declared twelve boxes of artificial silk on behalf of its customers, valued at more than 10,000 yuan. To evade taxes, the artificial silk was secretly stolen and replaced with straw and mud bricks. The scheme was discovered in Wenzhou. The original cargo has been returned to Shanghai. The Customs authority has ordered the Wanguo Express Warehouse Company, which originally made the declaration, to pursue the customer and send them to the Customs for handling. This matter was reported in this newspaper earlier. The counterfeit goods that were packed and shipped to various ports are being successively uncovered. Among them, those entrusted to the Ningshao Company's Xin Ningshao for shipment to Ningbo were handled in the same way. There were no consignee companies on the bill of lading. After receiving notifications from the Jianghai and Ouhai Customs, the Ningbo Customs opened the cargo and found that it was also straw and mud bricks, the same as those sent to Wenzhou. Those bound for Hankou and Tianjin and other ports will also be verified and returned to Shanghai in the next day or two. Currently, various shipping companies are pursuing Mr. Zhu of Wanguo Express Warehouse Company for the customs duties and round-trip shipping costs for the twelve boxes of artificial silk. It is reported that although the Express Company has determined that the goods were sold by Hengyuanxiang to merchants, the names of the buyers could not be found, so the tax evaders have not yet been found.

Military Band Performances Still Held at Zhaofeng Park

The drum corps of the 2nd Battalion of the British East Lancashire Regiment stationed in Shanghai is scheduled to perform at Zhaofeng Park on Tuesday, July 25, before "Retirement Opening". Although there was talk of a pause, arrangements have been made to proceed as originally planned. This performance will begin at 5:30 PM. The band will consist of 56 members.

Barbershop Industry Discusses the Tragic Cases of Gao and Zhu

＝The Zhu Case Has Begun＝

The Gao Case Has Temporarily Concluded

The Shanghai Barber Industry Committee for the Vindication of the Tragic Cases of Gao and Zhu held its 15th committee meeting on the morning of the day before yesterday at 10 AM. The committee members present were Luo Shantao, Qian Shuling, Wei Guoxian, Chen Sijiang, Pan Zhensan, Chen Youshou, Yang Jinxi, Xue Guangzhan, Guan Zhihe, and others, totaling eighteen. The family members of Gao Yuanlin and Zhu Chunjin also attended. Standing committee member Chen Sijiang was elected chairman. After the formalities, (A) matters were reported. 1. Regarding the Gao case negotiation, Luo Shantao and other representatives who went to Du's residence reported that Mr. Du had agreed to be responsible for mediating the Gao case and that a satisfactory result could be expected. The committee should wait quietly for the mediation. 2. Regarding the case of Zhu Ronghai, a fellow barber who was fatally injured by an American soldier in a car accident on July 5, the victim's father, Zhu Chunjin, had sent a letter to the committee requesting vindication. The victim's father, as a representative witness, Yan Ajin, had personally witnessed the American soldier's collision. A detailed report was also given regarding the court's investigation and trial. (B) Matters for discussion: 1. Regarding the Gao case, it was decided to wait quietly for Mr. Du's mediation. Further discussions would be held after the results were available. The victim's father, Gao Yuanlin, was temporarily provided with funds by the committee to return home and manage family affairs. Mr. Du provided 100 yuan, which was temporarily stored with the owner of Hushun Yuan Tang store. However, a receipt must be issued and kept by the committee, pending further arrangements when the case is completely resolved. 2. Regarding the case of Zhu Ronghai being killed by an American soldier, the following resolutions were made: 1. The committee would hire lawyer Yu Xiuying to handle the case according to law. 2. The committee would publicly elect two committee members, Qian and Wei, to contact Mr. Zhang Shangyi for mediation. 3. The committee would send a letter to the American Consulate, forwarding it to the American military camp officer, requesting generous compensation for the victim's family, in order to maintain the friendly relations between China and the United States. 4. Measures to provide relief for the victim's family would be discussed when the case has a satisfactory resolution. However, the victim's father is currently in financial difficulty, and the committee will provide appropriate relief. 3. Regarding the publication of a newspaper, it was decided to continue. However, the purpose is to promote the industry, so it was named "Rongguang" (容光). It was decided to publish it on the 5th. Industry members who have opinions to express should submit their manuscripts within three days for editing and publication. 4. The chairman reported briefly on the donations and expenditures of the various industry members this week. The meeting adjourned at 12 noon. After the meeting, committee member Qian and others accompanied the victim's father, Zhu Chunjin, to lawyer Yu Xiuying's office to sign a power of attorney in preparation for legal negotiations.

Wusong Office of the Health Bureau to Lay Foundation Stone Today

丨Mayor Wu Will Personally Preside Over Everything丨

The Wusong Office of the Health Bureau of this city has been under construction since last month. The preliminary work has now been completed in order. The Bureau originally scheduled the foundation stone laying ceremony for the 8th of this month, but it was postponed because Mayor Wu had not returned from Jiangxi. The Bureau has now rescheduled it for 2 PM today in Wusong. Mayor Wu will personally preside over the foundation laying. The details are as follows:

Brief History of Construction

Wusong's health facilities began in 1929. Because students from the Medical College of the National Central University joined in cooperation for on-site learning, everything progressed well. Unfortunately, the Shanghai Incident suddenly occurred, and it was destroyed by artillery fire. After the Shanghai War ended, although the Wusong District suffered from the ravages of war, residents continued to return, and the market gradually recovered. Li Yan'an, Director of the Health Bureau, recognized the importance of health protection in the district and, after repeated requests from citizens to restore these facilities for the sake of hygiene, specially petitioned the city government to find ways to restore them. Funds of 32,000 yuan were raised from the war zone's racetrack relief fund, and the Ministry of Health of the Interior approved a subsidy of more than 5,000 yuan. The National Tongji University also joined in cooperation for the convenience of its students' internships, and further helped to raise several thousand yuan in funding. In addition, the Jidetang, the former owner of the Wusong Seaside Hospital site, was negotiated to lease four acres and three points of public land to the Health Bureau for the construction of offices and hospitals at the lowest price. The Wusong Municipal Committee also strongly supported it. The Health Bureau then made proper plans, and the Boundary Affairs Bureau undertook it, beginning construction in early last month.

Foundation Stone Laying Today

After the Wusong Office of the Health Bureau

was built at the beginning of last month, the

preliminary project will be completed next time.

The contractor is Qiao Yuxing Construction Factory. The Bureau originally scheduled the foundation stone laying ceremony for the 8th of this month, but it was postponed because Mayor Wu had not returned from Jiangxi. Now that Mayor Wu has returned to Shanghai, the Bureau specifically scheduled the foundation stone laying for 2 PM today. Mayor Wu will personally preside over everything. Those who will participate at that time include important officials from the Municipal Government and various bureaus, members of the Municipal Committee of the District, and members of the medical community. All sectors are invited to attend the ceremony. The Bureau has issued 300 invitation cards yesterday.

Organizational Situation

After the foundation stone laying ceremony is held,

various projects will be actively carried out. It is

expected to be completed by the end of September

of this year. After various arrangements and equipment, the

office will officially open around New Year's Day next year. The internal organization

is divided into two departments: prevention and treatment. The plans are novel and all equipment

is improved, becoming a model for health equipment in various districts of the city. The method is that under the joint guidance of the Municipal Health Bureau and Tongji University, a health committee is established as a deliberative body, and a health office is established as an executive body. It is expected that the health undertakings in the district will have special progress.

Temporary Facilities

Until the new houses in the Wusong area are completed,

the health facilities before were

borrowed from Tongji University for several

rooms to serve as temporary offices, so that the citizens of the area can have hygiene guarantees. In view of the importance of hygiene this summer, the temporary office has been open since the 1st of this month.

Penalties for Privately Established Radio Stations

＝In Addition to Confiscating All Equipment,

a Fine of 1,200 Yuan＝

The International Telecommunications Bureau of the Ministry of Transportation in this port pays great attention to radio broadcasting and cracking down on privately established radio stations. The Bureau has recently discovered interference with broadcasting on its listening equipment. After investigation, it was found that someone in the area of Nine Acres in this city had privately established a radio station, broadcasting programs and communicating privately with radio stations in other ports. Yesterday, the Bureau sent a letter to the Municipal Public Works Bureau and the Municipal Public Security Bureau, requesting them to send personnel and police to search the building above the Tongxin Rice Shop at No. 85 Dajing Road and seize a transmitter. Zhang Jiaying, the person in charge of the privately established radio station, was taken to the Public Security Bureau for questioning. According to his confession, he did indeed privately establish the station. In addition to calling other stations for testing in the morning, there were no other uses. He asked for leniency. He also confessed that he had previously set up a radio station with his friends Mr. Cao and Mr. Fang, and they communicated with each other, naming it the "Meteor Radio Station". The two radio stations have now been dismantled, etc. It is reported that this case violated the Provisional Regulations for the Prohibition of Public Radio Stations of the Ministry of Transportation. In addition to confiscating all the equipment, a fine of 1,200 yuan will be imposed as a warning. It is also reported that the International Telecommunications Bureau is still conducting a thorough investigation to see if there are other privately established radio stations and strictly cracking down on them.

Shanghai Municipal Council Pays Attention to Summer Disease Prevention

Recently, the weather in Shanghai has been hot, with the temperature often exceeding 90 degrees. The Shanghai Municipal Council in the International Settlement is paying close attention to summer hygiene and disease prevention. According to news from the Council yesterday, doctors believe that most cases of heatstroke are caused by exposure through the eyes and back of the head. Preventive measures for heatstroke and other diseases include: 1) wearing a hat, 2) wearing sunglasses, 3) eating less, 4) wearing less clothing, and 5) keeping bowel movements regular. In addition, those who do not have the opportunity to exercise should eat even less.

Bandit Leader Hidden in Cargo Hold Finally Caught by Detectives

The detective team of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, on May 20 of this year, arrested Zhang Xiaoping from Yong, Guan Heshang from Wuxi, Wang Yulin from Qingjiang, Chen Xiaobao, Wang Azhang from Changshu, and Shen Jigang from Qingjiang, six bandits involved in the robbery of the Yifeng cigarette paper store on Taiping Bridge in the French Concession and the Cai Chang vegetable market in Sanwanli, Zhabei, in April of this year, in room 7 of the Xinkang Inn, Xin'an Lane, Jisi Fei'er Road, and confiscated three handguns and twenty-three bullets. At the same time, they also captured the principal offender, Qian Genfa (nicknamed Wu Xiangong) from Changshu, and his accomplice Wang Ruisheng at 14 Yifeng Lane on the same road. They also apprehended Liu Xitang from Henan and Zhu Agou and Zhu Zhangshi, a couple from the local area, at 15 Zhuangjia Lane, Xiaoyang Bridge, Caojiadu, bringing the total number of people arrested to eleven. However, after questioning, they all confessed that the principal offender was Zhou Jiangjiang (nicknamed Xiao Lan Jiao A Da), who was still at large. After repeated investigations, it was discovered that Zhou was from Zhenhai, 32 years old, and a well-known bandit leader who had committed numerous crimes in the Chinese and French concessions. Since the case was solved, he fled to Hankou to avoid punishment. On the 9th of this month, he secretly returned to Shanghai from Hankou and borrowed four yuan from a friend at the Xin Zha Bridge, planning to return to Hankou on the original ship yesterday. However, because the plan was not secret, Captain Lu discovered it and ordered several detectives to go to the Ning Shao Wharf in Nanshi at 4:00 a.m. yesterday, together with the relevant district headquarters, to wait. Unexpectedly, the bandit was very alert and had already bribed the waiter to hide in the cargo hold at the stern, covered with miscellaneous items and sacks, and sealed off externally. After the detectives explained their intentions to the comprador, the hold was unsealed, and Zhou was captured on the spot, immediately taken back to the team for interrogation.

Chauffeur Seduces Young Mistress and Flees with Her

Gong Bojian, a 42-year-old man from Qingpu who works as a coolie foreman (commonly known as a "jian tou") in the Caojiadu area, resides at 1 Xingyi Lane, Fuchun Street, Fangbang Road, Nanshi. Gong's wife, Lin, gave birth to a son named Yinbo, 21 years old, who works as a foreign coppersmith. Gong is by nature thrifty and has accumulated some savings. Because he works daily from Nanshi to Caojiadu, a long distance, he prepared a car for transportation, hiring Yao Guanchang (38 years old) as a chauffeur. However, in March of the twelfth year of the Republic of China, Gong was persuaded by a friend to give a seven-year-old girl named A Ying from Ling Dongsheng to Gong as a child bride. When A Ying turned seventeen, Gong married her to his son Yinbo on December 11 two years ago. The young couple initially lived in harmony. Unexpectedly, on May 6 of this year, when Mr. and Mrs. Gong went to Hangzhou for sightseeing, A Ying was left at home to watch over the house. At that time, the chauffeur Yao Guanchang saw A Ying alone and harbored malicious intentions, seducing her in every way possible and eventually developing a relationship. They often secretly met in inns, and before Mr. and Mrs. Gong returned from Hangzhou, he incited A Ying to take cash, silver dollars, and jewelry, worth about five hundred yuan, and eloped to Zhuganwei, outside the West Gate of Songjiang, where they lived together as husband and wife. When Gong returned from his trip, the people were gone and the money was gone. He filed a report with the Public Security Bureau requesting an arrest. Until recently, it was discovered that the adulterer Yao Guanchang had come to Shanghai alone and was hiding at 30 Yaojiazhai, Hongqiao Road. Captain Lu ordered detectives to arrest Yao at that address, and at the same time, sent personnel to Songjiang to arrest A Ying. They were sent to Shanghai yesterday to be interrogated.

River Dredging in War Zone Unearths Ammunition, Injuring Workers

The silt accumulation in rivers such as the Lu Jingpu and Shen Jin Gang in Zhabei has increased day by day. In addition, there are dangerous items left over from the war. The Post-War Rehabilitation Association of the Songhu War Zone of the National Government allocated funds for dredging, which has been completed one after another. Some of the finishing works are still being carried out by mechanical excavation. At around 10:00 a.m. yesterday, six or seven bombs were excavated. When worker Gu Menggen was transporting them to the Jiyang Bridge River Dredging Office, he accidentally triggered the mechanism due to improper handling, injuring his left foot. Personnel from the Engineering Office sent him to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment. It is said that his left foot needs to be amputated, which could lead to disability.

Seller of Opium Sentenced to Six Months' Imprisonment

丨Stealing Opium Results in 20 Days of Detention丨

Yesterday morning at 1:50 a.m., Gan Chenghua, a Hunanese opium vendor, was found carrying forty taels of opium with the intention of selling it. He was on his way to the home of a relative on Tao Peng Road, but he was unfamiliar with the route. As he was wandering around on Weituoma Road in Yangshupu, Ji Xigen from Tongzhou noticed that his abdomen was bulging and knew that he was carrying something. He went up and asked where he wanted to go. Gan said that he did not know the way. Ji then offered to guide him. However, after walking a few steps, Ji suddenly asked, "What exactly are you carrying? Take it out immediately!" He also pointed to a Mr. Jia standing nearby, saying that he was a plainclothes patrolman from the police station. However, Gan Chenghua firmly refused. Ji slapped Gan in the face, leading to a dispute. Two Chinese constables from the nearby No. 46 and other stations heard the commotion and rushed over, taking Gan and Ji to the police station. Forty taels of opium were found on Gan. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Local Court. Judge Wu Zehan presided over the trial. Police station lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated the case. Then, two Chinese constables reported the situation of the investigation and presented the opium for inspection. Gan Chenghua confessed that he came to Shanghai from Chongqing and that the opium was owed to him by a friend surnamed Chen for sixty yuan. He could not get the money back, so he brought the opium to sell for ten yuan. On the way, he met Ji Xigen, who wanted to rob him of the opium under the pretext of guiding him. Ji Xigen's confession was evasive. After reviewing the confessions, Judge Wu sentenced Gan Chenghua to six months' imprisonment and Ji Xigen to twenty days' detention. The opium was confiscated.

Woman's Legs Injured by Car, Husband Sues for Compensation

Wang Gengsheng, a local chauffeur, was driving a No. 16,501 cargo truck on Labor Sheng Road in West Shanghai on the 24th of last month when Sun Lin Shi, a Ningbo woman, was carrying a bamboo basket to the vegetable market to buy vegetables. As she was walking in the area, she was knocked down and her legs were injured by the front wheel of the truck. Chinese Constable No. 2,414 saw this and sent the injured woman to Guangci Hospital for treatment. At the same time, he reported the witnessed situation of Wang Gengsheng's careless accident causing injury to the Putuo Road Police Station for investigation. Sun Lin Shi has been hospitalized for treatment for over ten days, and her legs have not yet healed. According to the doctor's diagnosis, it is difficult to save the toes of both feet, so they have been amputated. Sun's husband said that because she is not yet forty years old, even if she recovers, she will be disabled. Wang Gengsheng is truly responsible for negligence of duty, so he hired lawyer Lin Jiching on behalf of his wife to file a criminal lawsuit against the driver with the First Special District Local Court, requesting that he be punished according to the law and that he compensate for all losses. However, Wang Gengsheng believes that the accident was caused by Sun Lin Shi's own carelessness, and he should not be solely responsible. Therefore, he also hired lawyers Ye Shaoying and Yang Linzhi to defend him. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Xiangzu opened the court for trial. Sun Lin Shi was unable to appear in court, so lawyer Lin stated the plaintiff's intentions and the circumstances of the accident on her behalf, and submitted a map of the accident site to the court. Afterwards, Chinese Constable No. 2414 came to court to testify, saying that although the defendant was not driving fast at the time, he did not hear him sound the horn, etc. Wang Gengsheng confessed that he had already sounded the horn at the time, but because the woman had already crossed in front of the car and suddenly retreated, his car could not avoid it. Judge Wu said that it was necessary to interrogate the victim in order to clarify the facts of the case, and that it was necessary to have the victim come to court in person to have the injuries examined by a forensic doctor. Therefore, the court decided to reschedule the trial for the afternoon of July 27.

Three Dead in Tragic Incidents

Beaten to Death: Yang Zhu Shi, a woman from Tangqiao Township, Pudong, was suspected of stealing plants by neighbors He Miaogen and his wife two months ago and was severely beaten by them.

Yang Zhu Shi filed a complaint with the local court, which found He Miaogen guilty and fined him. Hanged: An unidentified male corpse was found hanging from a jujube tree outside Zhenru yesterday morning. He was about 30 years old, wearing a white vest, blue cloth trousers, black socks, and black shoes. It is not known who he was. His suicide was probably due to desperation. He was spotted by local residents who reported it to the Third Precinct of the Fourth District, ordering them to urge an investigation to determine if he had any family members. Therefore, the case was reported to the local court for an autopsy.

Fell to Death: Li Baozhang, a 63-year-old man from Shandong, residing at No. 179 Luban Road, outside the West Gate, got up early yesterday morning to take a leisurely walk. Unexpectedly, after taking only a few steps out the door, he tripped on a stone step and fell forward. After falling, he never got up and died on the spot. The police officer reported the incident to the Second District Police Station, ordering the local security officer Gu Lan to report to the local court for an autopsy. However, the deceased's nephew, Li Yiyou, filed a request with the court to be exempted from the autopsy.

Medical and Pharmaceutical Industries

Benevolent Deed of the Citizen Association on Fourth Horse Road The 20th Branch of the Shanghai Special District Citizens' Federation sets up tea buckets on each section of the road (Fourth Horse Road) during the summer season to meet the needs of coolies who are thirsty. It also distributes various seasonal epidemic medicines within the association (Fuxiangli, Fourth Horse Road) to help the poor and sick. The association has also received large quantities of seasonal epidemic medicines donated by Wuzhou Music House Chinese and English Pharmacy, Zhongxi Pharmacy, and Puyi Pharmaceutical Company, and it is said that sick families can go and get them. The Shanghai Lianyi Charity Association Dispensary The temporary epidemic clinic attached to the Shanghai Lianyi Charity Association Dispensary at the corner of Disiwei Road and Dongyouheng Road, Hongkou, provides daily medical services and medicines to benefit the poor and sick. This session has been open since July 10, and the number of people seeking treatment is increasing daily. The hospital has hired doctors such as He Juju, Wu Zhankang, Pu Songzhou, Zhang Jisheng, Zhang Yaoqing, Pan Zhicheng, Songxia, and Feng Yinsheng to take charge of various departments.

Zhao's Father and Son Clinic Mr. Zhao Shiding, a giant of the People's Party, devoted himself to the revolution in his early years and has continued to help others. In the past ten years, he has abandoned his political career and devoted himself to the art of medicine. Mr. Zhao's medical knowledge is profound because it has been passed down from his ancestors for five generations. Those who seek treatment from him all find that his hands bring them back to life. This summer, Zhao's Father and Son Clinic has moved from its original location in Haimen to No. 2 Shuangwen Lane, Dushan Father Road, Xiqiao, specializing in traumatology, internal medicine, gynecology, pediatrics and other diseases. It also carefully selects good medicines and makes pills, powders, ointments and plasters that are easy to take and have significant effects.

Scrofula Specialist Zhu Shaoyun Opens Night Clinic Zhu Shaoyun, a Suzhou scrofula specialist doctor, whose family has been practicing medicine for generations, with profound medical knowledge and superb skills, specializes in the treatment of various scrofula on the neck and has considerable experience. His clinic hours are from 10:00 a.m. to 3:00 p.m. Recently, due to the hot weather, in order to facilitate patients, a special night clinic will be open for two hours, scheduled from 6:00 p.m. to 8:00 p.m., and those who are late will not be seen.

Dr. Wang Zanshu's Clinic Relocates Wang Zanshu, a famous doctor from Xin'an, came to Shanghai from Jiangxi in the 20th year of the Republic of China to avoid bandits and set up a clinic in Hongxiang Lane, Xin Zha Road. In the past three years, the clinic has been very successful. All those who have been treated by Dr. Wang have found that his hands bring them back to life. As a result, his reputation has risen, and the number of people seeking treatment has increased, so the original house is not sufficient. A three-bay house has been specially built at No. 4 Dashun Lane at the intersection of Tibet Road (i.e., north of the epidemic hospital) as a new clinic, telephone number 92661. It is said that he has moved in and will continue to see patients as usual from the first of this month.

Calligraphy and Painting News

Joint Calligraphy and Painting Exhibition by Zhao and Lin Zhao Huiqing and Lin Jianxing, calligraphers and painters from Eastern Zhejiang, are proficient in the four scripts and elegant in the six principles of painting. They are also capable of engraving. Zhao's calligraphy is calm and unrestrained, drawing on Pu Tang, and directly pursuing the Qin and Han dynasties, especially in seal script. Lin's landscapes, figures, and animals are unique and show that he has fully explored the mysteries of the ancients without falling into the clichés of his predecessors, which is especially commendable. The two held an exhibition in Ningbo once last year, which was greatly praised by the people of Ningbo. They have now presented more than a hundred recent works in a joint public exhibition on the 17th, 18th, and 9th of this month at the fourth floor of the Ningbo Township Association on Tibet Road. People in Shanghai should be able to feast their eyes.

Letter

To the Editor: Regarding the article published in your newspaper on July 13th, "Zhabei Silk Factory Strikes Again Yesterday," which stated that when the factory was about to pay the weekly wages, the workers claimed that according to the regulations, each person should receive 5 jiao 8 fen, but the factory only paid 5 jiao per worker. Therefore, they questioned the factory, but the factory replied that 8 fen of it was deducted at the request of the labor union to be handed over to the labor union, etc. This is inconsistent with the facts. The increase in wages to 5 jiao was decided by the Social Affairs Bureau through mediation. The workers may have misunderstood. How could our factory not guide them? Moreover, our factory did not pay any weekly bonuses or wages that day, and the workers did not ask about this. Their strike was due to believing rumors and misunderstandings. The Social Affairs Bureau and the 6th District Silk Industry Labor Union have sent people to explain in detail, and work has resumed as usual. Therefore, we specifically send this letter for correction and hope it will be published in the "Letters to the Editor" column. Yours respectfully, Ji Yu Tai Ji Silk Factory, July 14th.

Davis Cup

Great Britain in Advantage in European Zone Final

Crawford Wins Over Austin

Pan Rai Wins Over McGrath

| Great Britain Wins Doubles Against Australia |

(London, 13th, Reuters) The Davis Cup European Zone final between Australia and Great Britain has aroused great interest. The first two singles matches were played today. The winners of the Australian and British teams will compete against the United States in the inter-zone final, and then compete against France in the Challenge Round.

Victory Hangs on Doubles According to general observations, the success or failure of Great Britain and Australia will depend on the doubles match. Crawford, who defeated Barnes in Wimbledon to win the championship, first played against Austin. McGrath then met Pan Rai. Australian players expressed great optimism about the outcome of the match.

First Day Final

(London, 14th, Reuters) Results of the first day of the Davis Cup European Zone final: Crawford defeated Austin, McGrath lost to Pan Rai. Results are as follows:

Crawford (Australia) 4-6, 6-2, 6-2, 6-3 Austin (Great Britain)

Pan Rai (Great Britain) 6-2, 6-4, 6-2 McGrath (Australia)

Rain Delays Match by Half an Hour

Large Crowd Today

Gathered at the Central Court of Wimbledon to watch the two British Empire teams compete. However, the match was delayed by ninety minutes due to rain. During the intense match, the audience cheered and shouted, and the referee had to ask for silence.

Crawford Wins Over Austin

Australia's Wimbledon Champion Crawford's Killing Shots Are Terrible, But Every Point Won is Extremely Difficult. Austin is Especially Energetic, The Ball Has Unexpected Speed, And His Movements Are Fast, And He Should Save The Close Ball. Austin Fights With The Utmost Confidence, Unlike His Performance at Wimbledon.

Pan Rai Wins Over McGrath

McGrath's Defeat

Is Entirely Due to a Lack of Courage, His Striking is Panicked and Relaxed, Pan Rai is Both Powerful and Good at Killing, McGrath's Forehand is a Complete Failure, His Striking Is Not Good, and Mistakes Are Made Everywhere.

Second Day Final

Great Britain Wins Doubles (Reuters, London, 14th) In the Davis Cup European Zone Final, Great Britain won the doubles against Australia, 7-5, 6-4, 3-6, 6-3. Great Britain now leads 2-1, and it is not difficult to win the European Zone Championship.

Important News

Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education's Measures to Award and Assist Outstanding High School Entrance Examination Students to Enter Higher Education

Six Scholarships to Be Established: The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education's Interim Measures for Awarding and Assisting Outstanding High School General Course Graduation Examination Students to Enter Higher Education are as follows: 1. The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education has specially established six scholarships to award and assist high school general course graduation examination students to enter higher education. 2. The top six students who pass the high school general course graduation examination and are confirmed to be from this province, who are admitted to national universities or colleges that meet the requirements of Article 4, may receive scholarships, for a period of four years. 3. The scholarships mentioned in the preceding paragraph shall be limited to 300 yuan per person per year, and shall be issued by the Jiangsu Education Funding Management Office in two installments, spring and autumn. 4. Students who are admitted to the following departments may receive scholarships: A. Those admitted to various departments of the School of Science and Engineering; B. Those admitted to various departments of the School of Agriculture; C. Those admitted to the Accounting Department of the School of Commerce and the History and Geography Departments of the School of Liberal Arts. 5. Students who receive scholarships shall submit their academic performance to the school where they are located each semester and request the Department of Education to verify it. Those who repeat a grade will have their scholarship suspended from the next academic year. Those who suspend their studies due to illness or withdraw from school will have their scholarship suspended from the date of suspension or withdrawal. Those who violate school rules and are expelled from the school where they are located shall have the scholarships they have already received recovered from their guarantor. 6. The top six students who pass the graduation examination shall, after being admitted to national universities or colleges, submit their information through the school where they are located to the Department of Education for registration. 7. Students who receive scholarships shall find a reliable guarantor, fill out a letter of guarantee and submit it to the Department of Education for verification. Form of the letter of guarantee: Letter of Guarantee: Student ○○○ is from ○○ County, Jiangsu Province, ○○ years old, and is currently studying in the ○○○ Department of the ○○ College (or University). In accordance with the Interim Measures for Awarding and Assisting Outstanding High School General Course Graduation Examination Students to Enter Higher Education, they should receive a scholarship. It is hereby certified that if the student is subsequently expelled from school due to violation of school rules, they shall repay the scholarships they have already received. This certificate, with the signature and seal of the guarantor.

AC Hum in AC Radios

— Xiang

The biggest drawback of AC radios is that they are prone to humming (Hum). Although this humming cannot be completely eliminated, if designed properly, it can be reduced to a minimum so as not to interfere with reception.

Source 1. Due to insufficient capacitance or leakage of the filter capacitor in the power supply section, or the filter choke being too small.

2. Due to the loudspeaker. Because the magnetic field coil (Field Coil) of ordinary AC dynamic loudspeakers (DymaicSpeaker, commonly known as electric horn) also uses a filter choke, the pulsating DC current after rectification can often be induced into the voice coil (VoiceCoil), resulting in strong AC hum.

3. Due to other random electrostatic and magnetic field induction.

4. Sometimes, the live wire of the electric light introduces the signal voltage to the rectifier tube, which modulates with the output voltage, transmitting to various circuits of the radio, resulting in AC hum.

5. Sometimes, the alternating current field around the pole or cathode has the ability to control the screen current, so it can also generate a small amount of AC hum.

6. In indirectly heated vacuum tubes, the voltage between the cathode (Cathode) and the heater (Heater) is too high, causing leakage in the middle.

Inspection Method

To eliminate AC hum, the source must first be identified. The inspection steps are to short-circuit the input and output circuits of each stage in order to distinguish which stage the AC hum is generated in. If the AC hum cannot be eliminated when the input circuit of the last low-frequency amplification stage is short-circuited, then the obstacle is probably in the power supply section. If the AC hum continues to exist after the output transformer or the voice coil of the loudspeaker is short-circuited, it can be determined that it is due to the second type of source. As for the elimination method, I will discuss it in the next issue.

Talking About Loudspeakers (Continued)

— Yizhi

(3) Balanced Diaphragm Loudspeaker: This loudspeaker is a combination of bipolar and balanced armature types. It can also be said to be made of two bipolar types. Its simple structural principle is shown in Figure 4. MM is the magnet, C is the voice coil, and D is the diaphragm. Its sound amplification principle is the same as that of the balanced type. Its characteristics are (1) the balanced diaphragm always maintains its balanced position, so the reciprocating amplitude is always equal; (2) because a small magnet passes through part of the magnetic flux, the magnetism is not easily lost; (3) the magnetic field is not easily saturated, and the load current can be increased; (4) it does not generate double-frequency noise. Its use: similar to that of the balanced armature type, but this type is slightly more difficult to manufacture than the balanced armature type and the price is also slightly more expensive, so it is not as widely used as the balanced armature type.

(2) Moving Coil Loudspeaker:

The structural principle of the moving coil loudspeaker is slightly different from that of the fixed coil type. Its structure is based on the principle of a motor. When the moving coil is loaded with a sound wave current, a magnetic field is generated between the coils, which changes the attraction force with the parent magnetic field (this magnetic field is generated by introducing current to the excitation coil to create a strong electromagnetic field), pushing and pulling back and forth, vibrating and exciting the diaphragm to become a sound wave. A special feature of this loudspeaker is that the magnetic field does not use permanent magnets. However, because this type of loudspeaker needs to push a large diaphragm of the moving coil, a strong magnetic field is required. The magnetic field strength of a permanent magnet, for the same size, is always lower than that of an electromagnet. Its structure is shown in Figure 5: E is the magnet, C is the excitation coil, M is the moving coil, and D is the hollow conical diaphragm. When an external sound wave current is input into the moving coil, it changes the attraction force with the parent magnetic field, pushing the diaphragm and emitting sound. The advantages of this type of loudspeaker are (1) the diaphragm is not limited by the air gap, so the diaphragm amplitude can be expanded; (2) unlike the fixed coil type, it does not need a certain elasticity to maintain its working stability; (3) the current of the moving coil is completely proportional to the current that pushes this coil; (4) because the magnetic lines do not pass through the diaphragm, saturation does not occur. These are some of its advantages, but there are also several disadvantages: (1) the parent magnetic field needs a strong magnetic force, so the required magnet area is larger and the weight is increased; (2) it needs direct current to excite the magnetic force, so it consumes more power; (3) the structure is quite difficult and the price is more expensive than the fixed type. This type of loudspeaker is most suitable for use in powerful radios or amplifiers to be heard by dozens or hundreds or thousands of people. The AC radios and amplifiers in movie theaters on the market are all of this type. (To be continued)

Transformer Revival Method

— Zhi

Transformers are most easily damaged (the reasons are no more than two: one is that the load current is too large and the wire is broken, and the other is that moisture intrusion breaks the wire). After damage, replacing the new coil is almost the same price as buying a new one; if you disassemble and rewind, the procedures are cumbersome and only those with experience can do it. Therefore, when the transformer is damaged, it is often discarded and a new one is purchased. But now there is a simple repair method that can instantly restore the damaged transformer, just like performing a revival method on a vacuum tube. The method is as follows:

Connect the two poles (mostly the P pole and B pole) of the damaged transformer (specifically referring to audio transformers Audio transformer) with broken wires directly to a 220-volt voltage for about two or three seconds, which can naturally connect and revive the broken wires. If it doesn't work, continue the experiment like this once; if it doesn't work again, continue once more and extend the time slightly. If the transformer still cannot be revived after three such experiments, then the distance of the break in the transformer is too large to revive it, and it can only be disassembled and rewound.

Why can the broken wire of the transformer be naturally welded after connecting to a 220-volt voltage? This is the application of the principle of arc welding (ElectricaicWeldiidg). If you want to study it in depth, please refer to the electric welding method in any electrical engineering book.

The author once had two transformers, one with the positive loop burned out and one with mold breaking the wire. Both have been revived using this method. It has been used for more than four months now and has not been damaged. Those who have damaged transformers may wish to experiment.

Small Experience

— Ke Rongyan

(1) It is difficult to scrape off the paint on thin enameled steel wire. You can use a wire to burn the paint off on an alcohol lamp.

(2) The tin sheet of toothpaste tube is a good material for making fixed capacitors; the tin lid is also an excellent mineral cup.

(3) Hard cardboard soaked in candle oil and painted with paint is a good insulating board; broken phonograph records can also be used in the same way.

(4) Both ends of the rubber tube coil can be connected to two terminals, which can be convenient for loading and unloading.

(5) Two spider web coil boards are connected with a screw, and a spring from an old thermos bottle is sandwiched in the middle, which is a set of three-circuit coil racks. You can immediately wind the primary and secondary coils on the first board and the regenerative coil on the second board. Rotating the nut on the screw can finely adjust the regenerative force.

(6) Broken celluloid cigarette cases, soap boxes, etc. can be cut into small pieces and wound with resistance wires, etc. as insulators.

Self-Made Slow Rotation Dial

— Li Yuanqing

A radio with good selectivity, if there is a slight difference in adjustment, it cannot get sound. If you want to get accurate and convenient adjustment, you can't do without a slow rotation dial.

The slow rotation dial introduced in this article is very simple in structure, but it is also very convenient to use. First, tighten the bakelite top of the wiring stud tightly to prevent it from slipping out easily. Then put a small section of rubber tube on the bakelite top. Then drill a small hole in the plastic board, insert the wiring stud, put on the spring, and tighten it with two screw nuts. (As shown in the figure) Because the rubber tube has elasticity, it can be lubricated freely when rotating.

Timer Switch Made Using an Alarm Clock

— Li Qing

Many friends who play with the radio, because they are too fascinated, even if they are in bed, they are still reluctant to drop the earphones. But if you are not careful, you will fall asleep, and as a result, not only is the battery wasted, but the radio is also easily damaged because it is open for a long time. To avoid this loss, you have to install a timer switch.

Connect to A Battery or AC220V Radio

As shown in the figure, C is the alarm clock, W is the wooden strip, AB is the copper sheet, and D is the wooden piece. (Fixed in the small hole of the K key with screws) First set the alarm clock pointer to the time you want to stop, then when the K key reaches the predetermined time, it will rotate towards W, and at the same time, the two copper sheets AB can automatically disconnect the circuit because they have elasticity.

Note: If this device is used in an AC radio, all parts of the two copper sheets AB must be completely wrapped with cloth except for the contact points, otherwise it is easy to cause danger.

Common Knowledge

— Huang Jiancun

(10) Receiving Antenna and Ground Wire (1) The term "antenna," in English called "Antenna," originally should be interpreted as the antennae of an insect. Because an antenna uses a conductor suspended high in space to absorb radio waves, its function is quite similar to the antennae of an insect (commonly called "whiskers"), so people at the time used the name "Antenna" for antennae as the name for antennas.

A ground wire is a metal object buried in the ground to complete the antenna's circuit, allowing the received current to oscillate in the circuit and become the driving force of the radio.

Therefore, the quality of the antenna and ground wire has a great impact on the efficiency of radio reception. In particular, crystal radios, unlike vacuum tube radios, do not have amplification and can only use the current generated in the antenna directly as the driving force.

Therefore, the quality of the antenna and ground wire must be carefully considered.

(1) Antenna Shape: Although there are many shapes of antennas, there are several common types used for receiving broadcasts: (A) Inverted L-type antenna: As shown in the first diagram, this type of antenna suspends a horizontal wire between two bamboo poles, each end connected to a porcelain or glass insulator, and connects one end to a lead-in wire, leading to the radio indoors. Its shape is quite similar to an inverted letter "L," hence the name inverted L-type antenna. Figure 4

(B) T-type antenna: As shown in the second diagram, this type of antenna has the lead-in wire connected to the center of the horizontal wire, and its shape is quite similar to the letter "T."

(C) Inclined antenna: As shown in the third diagram, a conductor is mounted diagonally on a wooden pole.

Figure 3 Radio

(D) Loop antenna: As shown in the fourth diagram, this type of antenna is made by winding about a hundred feet of insulated conductor wire into a square. It has excellent directivity and is often used in high-end radios with excellent sensitivity.

In diagrams, the symbol for an antenna, regardless of its shape, is often

Figure 2 Radio

or , but for a loop antenna, the symbol is Figure 1 Radio

(2) Antenna Height: The higher the antenna is erected, the greater the voltage it receives, and the sensitivity of the radio (Sensitivity) also increases greatly. However, the higher the antenna, the more difficult it is to handle. Generally, for receiving broadcasts, a height of about seven to ten meters is used, and the length of the horizontal part is about the same as the height or twice that number is more suitable.

(3) Antenna Position: If there are electric lights, power lines, or telegraph and telephone lines near the antenna, the antenna will be affected, and the sensitivity of the radio will be reduced. Therefore, the antenna must be at least three meters away from power lines, etc., and at least six meters away from high-voltage lines.

Difficult problems can be solved. In addition, if there is any damage within one year, it can be repaired free of charge. The service can be called thoughtful, making it the best in the market.

Spring and Autumn

Filial Son Keeping Watch Over the Tomb

— Shanlu

Nouns are related to the times; good nouns in ancient times can become dirty nouns in modern times. Ancient sex books must be read solemnly; modern sex books have become a medium for inciting lewdness. Ancient sages were revered and supreme titles; modern sages have become terms of ridicule. Recently, many filial sons keeping watch over tombs have emerged in Henan. Looking at it with old eyes, the system of guarding the tomb for about three years has been revived, which can expand the Twenty-four Filial Piety into Twenty-five Filial Piety. If Zuo Qiuming were reborn in this world, he would definitely sing his praises, saying: "The Book of Songs says, 'Filial sons are never exhausted, and their kind will be blessed forever.' Is this what it means?"

However, after investigating the truth about the filial sons guarding the tomb, alas! Their ancestors of the seventeenth generation are truly unfortunate to have these filial sons guarding the tomb! It turns out that Anyang, Henan, known as the ancient Yin Ruins, has been the site of continuous excavation work since the Academia Sinica once excavated it. As soon as colorful ancient artifacts appear, many antique ghosts, like flies attached to dung, follow them. Commonly known as "digging up ancestors' graves," it means digging up other people's ancestral graves. Now, people in Anyang are digging up their own ancestral graves. If no one is watching during the excavation, they will inevitably be swallowed up by the servants. Therefore, descendants digging up ancestral graves are regarded as a rare commodity to be hoarded, and the landowner must supervise the excavation. The servants call these supervising landowners "filial sons guarding the tomb." As a result, many filial sons guarding the tomb, who brave the frost and snow and do not fear the wind and rain, have suddenly been added to the tombs in Anyang. How filial are the people of Anyang! How filial are the people of Anyang! With these filial sons guarding the tomb, the good word "filial piety" has been corrupted by later generations. The "anti-filial piety faction" once said, "Of all evils, filial piety is the head." These five words are indeed an overstatement, but they are perfectly suited to the filial sons guarding the tomb in Anyang and do not feel excessive at all.

The Japanese's Search

— Sisu

The Japanese have been collecting Chinese antiques for a long time. Many Chinese cultural relics have been transported overseas to the east and stored in Japanese official and private collections. It is unknown how many there are. By now, it seems that the valuable antiques have been collected almost completely, and there is gradually nothing left to collect. Therefore, they have had to expand the scope of their search, not limited to the ancient, but also including the modern, not limited to rare treasures, but also including trivial things. Anything that China does not have much of is included in the search. The antiques passed down from ancient times are ultimately limited. When the Japanese collect one item, China loses one item. Antiques cannot give birth to antiques. Imitations are copies, not antiques. The Japanese have exhausted all means, either secretly buying them, or forcibly buying them by relying on their power, such as buying the Qin and Han bricks and tiles and stone Buddhas from a certain family a few years ago; or they have resorted to military occupation, such as all the antiques in the four northeastern provinces, which have become prisoners. Shenyang has the Forbidden City, and Rehe has the Imperial Villa. The antiques here are especially abundant, and the Japanese have collected them most happily and satisfactorily. However, the more the Japanese collect, the more China lacks, like a lamp that has run out of oil. Where else can they collect? We know that there are several Chinese rare books in Japanese libraries. Chinese people cannot see books written by Chinese people, but they flow into Japanese libraries instead. The Japanese are so proud of this, and the Chinese are so frustrated! However, the so-called rare books are ultimately only a few. If the Chinese also have them stored, they are not rare books and are not precious enough. If they are still limited to antiques, they will be laboring in vain. The clever Japanese have expanded the scope of their search.

The expansion began on September 18 of the year before last. Just look: since 9/18, the rare Chinese items collected in Changchun are so abundant. How many Zheng Xiaoxus can be found in such a large China? Regarding rarity as precious, after the Japanese began to expand the scope, they regarded "rarity" as the condition for all searches. Anything rare in China is regarded as precious as an antique, regardless of whether the Chinese consider it smelly or rotten, they all regard it as magical and happily collect it endlessly. Therefore, even gangsters are treasured this year. Who knows what else will be taken away in the future!

Random Talk About Cartoons

— (Qian Yun writes, Dong Liang draws)

Big Shanghai?

Why are the streets of Shanghai so crowded lately? They were driven out by bedbugs! Most of them. Often more than ten families live in one house. To put it bluntly, people live inside like steamed buns in a steamer, cooked by the fire. Cold days are okay, but hot days are

It's killing people; so they eat in the open air, sleep in the open air, and even excrete in the open air. The open air is the world of people in the steamer, and the world is their sky. They sleep on the ground and are covered by the sky. It's great!

Shanghai is really an amazing place (so those who write in English say that this kind of pronunciation is loud, and I will borrow it here to show its amazingness), otherwise why do people from all over the world come in droves, sometimes even squeezing some people into the Huangpu River? In fact, not only are the houses crowded, but even food is not available; unfortunately, most people still don't believe this, thinking that Shanghai is such a big place.

The Life of a Goddess

— Bing Ding

An ancient poet said: "Don't say that human beings are like mandarin ducks, I will look at them as wailing geese." This is what the ancients wrote when lamenting prostitutes. I often daydream, thinking that a good woman, why would she willingly become a prostitute? Is it for poverty? There are many occupations for women, so why bother with this kind of physical life? Is it for comfort? Working under the stars and moon, serving people with trepidation, is not necessarily a spiritually peaceful life. However, they enjoy it tirelessly, and are willing to live this kind of "inhuman life," which is really puzzling.

It's not that I'm negating the current prostitutes, thinking that there are also those with good character, and their beauty may not be inferior to that of the ancients. However, the prostitutes of the past often had skills besides their appearance, such as poetry, painting, and music, all of which were well-established. What about now? Singing a few Peking operas, dancing, flirting, riding in cars, and eating big dishes are all they know. Once they open their mouths, most of them are like hooligans, tricksters, or maybe superficial Europeans. Embroidered pillows, I really dare not compliment them.

During the Song Dynasty, Liang Hongyu was able to recognize Han Shizhong and help her husband defeat the Jin people. When Su Dongpo was in Hangzhou, the prostitute Zhou Shao wrote a poem and asked to be removed from the register: "The nest on the beam is empty, and the years are alarming. Looking back, I comb my wings. If you release the white-clothed woman from the cage, I will always recite the Avalokiteśvara Prajñā Sutra."

Li Shishi was able to overthrow the Daoist monarch, not necessarily because of her appearance, but probably because her skills were superior. Although the officials of the Ming Dynasty indulged in pleasure, it was indeed a sign of national subjugation; however, these Chen Yuanyuan, Liu Rushi, Dong Xiaowan, and Li Xiangjun must also have had many special talents to be able to become demons of national subjugation. Today's prostitutes are probably not up to that level. For example, the famous Sai Jinhua, does she know poetry? Does she know painting? She's just romantic. Since Kuai, it's really hard to find a singer from the Ming Dynasty. For example, if someone wants to write a modern "Biography of Famous Prostitutes," it will be as difficult as writing a modern "Biography of Honest Officials." Going to brothels is an elegant thing, not a vulgar thing. Because sexual comfort is enough to regulate a lonely life, it cannot be said that a person who goes to brothels without being chaotic is a bad thing. However, judging from the current situation, unless one is ignorant, who dares to say that "the world is turbid?" Where can we talk about "elegance"? As for other places where flesh is bought and sold, it is really an expression of bestiality. I call them "wailing geese" because of my compassion!

Whereabouts

Travel Notes of the World's Fair (4)

— Huang Juemin

(5) Aerial Wire Bridge (Figure 3) is 1,850 feet long and 638 feet high. There is a viewing platform on top, and a steel car weighing 220,000 pounds is suspended in the middle. It can carry 5,000 passengers per hour, going straight from one end to the other. Unfortunately, this bridge was not yet in operation during my two days of visiting the fair, so I did not have the opportunity to visit it in person, which I deeply regret. But only seven days after leaving, I received a radio message on the President Jackson ship on the Pacific Ocean, saying that a sudden gale that day caused great panic to those who climbed the bridge, and I couldn't help but rejoice in my good fortune.

(6) Antarctic Exploration Ship (Figure 4) The ship is made entirely of wood and is not large in scale. Sails and machines were used during navigation. It was used by the American explorer Byrd in 1926 to explore Antarctica. The ship displays all the equipment Byrd brought with him during his exploration. In the autumn of 1931, I personally witnessed Byrd's demeanor and the Antarctic exploration films he shot at the Universal Apartments in New York. Now this ship has become a historical treasure, so I also record it to show the difficulty of a small ship exploring great dangers.

In addition, there are many places in the fair dedicated to entertainment, such as magic tricks, steamer rides, watching big snakes, dwarfs, etc. Because they are products attached to the fair and the time is short, I had to skip them. Even what I have recorded above is only a general situation, and I dare not say it is detailed.

5. Other Miscellany

(1) World's Largest Thermometer The thermometer is 200 feet high, and the numbers in the thermometer are 10 feet high each. It is built from 10 miles of wire and 60 tons of steel plates and is called the Chicago Climate Monument. Whether day or night, the temperature can be seen from all parts of the fair.

(2) Art Exhibition Hall Exhibits art works worth more than 75 million gold dollars. It was collected and borrowed from 25 famous museums and 250 art collections around the world.

(3) Science Congress Launched by the American Association for the Advancement of Science and the World's Fair. The conference period is set from June 19 to June 30. Science giants are invited to visit and hold a conference.

(4) Various Sports Competitions Various track and field, ball games, swimming, boating, etc., are held from May 10 to June 10. Most of the ball games are played at the Chicago Fallen Soldiers Memorial Stadium. The stadium is the largest stadium in the world and can accommodate 100,000 spectators.

Free Talk

Textbook Dump

— Zhu

Every year, I only see the price of books that "spread culture" rising. First, the original price was sold at an 80% discount, but now it is sold at the actual price; then the actual price has risen by another 10% or 20%; the reason is that the cost is expensive and the expenses are huge. Unexpectedly, at the beginning of this summer, I suddenly saw several large bookstores posting large-scale advertisements, selling textbooks at a low price: middle school textbooks that were originally sold at the actual price were reduced to 80% of the price, and elementary school textbooks that were originally sold at an 80% discount were reduced to 60% of the price! Textbooks are necessities for students, and although a 20% discount is not a large amount, poor students have actually benefited a lot. On this point, everyone should welcome the big price reduction of textbooks. The editing and printing of primary and secondary textbooks was only done by three major bookstores, Commercial Press, China Bookstore, and World Bookstore, four or five years ago; these three "divided" China's "educational world." They each have "spheres of influence," and although they are "divided," they also "cooperate." It is said that a large amount of capital is required to edit and print primary and secondary textbooks, and it is also said that there must be "clues" to promote textbooks; it is really a big deal, and ordinary bookstores dare not take it upon themselves. Moreover, since "the world" has been determined to be "three," it is even more difficult for other companies to open up a path. However, in the past three or four years, bookstores have also risked engaging in textbooks because there are few "ways out" in business. To date, several companies, including Kaiming, Shenzhou, Beixin, and Dadong, have compiled middle school textbooks. However, it is said that the "basic territory" of textbooks is not in "middle" but in "small." Therefore, two more companies, Kaiming and Dadong, have also added the editing and printing of elementary school textbooks. Now there are five kinds of elementary school textbooks placed in front of elementary school teachers for them to choose and adopt. The big price reduction of textbooks has therefore occurred. According to ordinary habits, if a new cloth shop opens on a street and reduces prices, the old-brand cloth shops on the same street will inevitably also reduce prices greatly. Although bookstores say they are "serving culture," they can hardly escape this iron rule of business competition. In this competition, shops with weak capital and inflexible skills will inevitably suffer losses. This is another iron rule of commerce. However, textbooks are ultimately related to culture and cannot be compared with ordinary commodities; ordinary people also compare the quality of a foot of cloth, and now that they are special "commodities" related to children's education, they should naturally be compared. The right to choose naturally rests with the elementary school teachers. However, teachers who study elementary school education should also take advantage of this big sale to make a fair criticism of the books of each company and provide elementary school teachers with a reference for selection. Only in this way can the big sale of textbooks at a 60% discount not become a purely commercial competition, and then can it be said that it is truly beneficial to children.

In short, there is progress with competition, but shoddy products often become more rampant due to competition; therefore, impartial and just criticism is even more necessary!

Root

— Ye Rong

Root packed a few pieces of her own clothes. With tear-filled eyes, she pointed to a pile of ragged clothes on the bed and told me: these are Dad's, these are Little Four's, all mended. I'll keep a few pieces of my own clothes, and tomorrow I'll alter them for Little Four to wear. At this moment, tears fell from her face like a broken string of pearls, like rain.

I sighed and wanted to comfort her, but what could I say? What could I say? I had sold my own daughter as if she were a piece of rag. My throat felt choked, as if something was stuck in it, and I couldn't breathe. A layer of faint tears blurred my eyes. Root wiped her tears and went back and forth, tidying things up. It seemed she wanted to get everything in order so that I would never have to worry; it also seemed like she was saying goodbye to everything.

I sat in a daze, as if I were in a trance, not thinking anything, not saying anything. My heart was completely still.

Since her mother died, followed by years of floods and war, we couldn't harvest anything from the fields. The whole family was exhausted, struggling with hunger every day. Yet, things got worse day by day, and now I had to sell my gentle and sensible daughter to pay off our debts. Heaven, what kind of world is this?

Why was I so confused and sold her for eighty yuan? She is my daughter, my own flesh and blood!

But it's too late to regret it now. Didn't I accept ten yuan as a deposit?…

I couldn't help but recall her good qualities. Without her, how could we have survived these years of hardship? She managed the household, looked after her brothers, and sometimes had to endure my bad temper. A poor girl, not even sixteen, took on all the hardships her mother left behind. She had to go here and there to find food for herself and her brothers. She had to step forward with tears in her eyes, to listen to the insults of the debt collectors on my behalf, and to plead with them. She even had to… She had been my daughter for more than ten years, and never had a single good day. Now, I have to sell her to pay off debts! How can I go on living without her after I sell her and lose her?

Little Four ran in from outside, naked and covered in dust. Root pulled him towards her and then let him go. She said,

"Little Four, come wash up." After washing, I'll be gone. Who will wash you? "She immediately scooped a basin of water and began to wash him.

Little Four asked: "Where are you going? Can I go with you?"

Root lowered her head and answered him after a long time: she was going out to pick mud beans and he didn't need to go. Later, she whispered to him, telling him not to run around, to listen to Dad, and not to go with Wang Agui to the mud pit to bathe.

After washing Little Four, she took out a short shirt and put it on him, then led him to the kitchen. I couldn't help but feel heartbroken looking at her back. I raised my hand and thumped my chest a few times. I wished my body would explode and destroy the whole world…

After Root cooked lunch, we ate and cleaned up the dishes. After hesitating for a while, she asked me:

"Dad, am I leaving now? Didn't Uncle Zhou say that after we ate, Dad would take me?…" she said softly, but without crying. Her voice was like a sharp knife, each word cutting into my heart. How could I let her go? How could I personally lead her, lead my Root, to hand her over to someone else? After a moment of silence, I said:

"Don't go then. Root, don't go." The voice seemed to burst from my heart. She stared at me with both eyes, without a sound. Then I saw tears falling from her face like broken beads again. She covered her face and sobbed.

Zhou Baoxian suddenly stood at the door and said, "Let's go, it's getting late. Didn't I say we had to catch the bus today?"

A World Literary History in "Silhouette Collection"

— Can Yue

Recently, after finishing the History of the Development of European Literature and European Art of the Twentieth Century, I became quite interested in literary history. It just so happened that the Zhonghua Book Company was heavily advertising the "Guohuo" (National Product) World Literary History, volumes one and two, in neat columns of small type. In the "Collection of Praises," so-called famous scholars and experts were singing its praises (whether they were excerpts from letters is unknown), so I bought a copy to see the brilliant materialist research methods of Yu Mutao, this Chinese Sinclair disciple.

Opening the first page, in a preface, the opening line was "This is the saying of a 'great man'!" It scared me into a cold sweat. Who is this so-called great man? There are so many of them. It's just unsettling. Then, the author says a series of words about the Chinese publishing industry, which he finds unsatisfactory. The reason is that "there are virtually no decent works in the translation and writing of literary history." So he offers this "decent" world literary history.

It turns out that this book is written based on two "famous sayings." It startled me again: What are these "famous sayings?" They are:

"Literature is a reflection of social life."

"Only with the October Revolution was there modern Russian literature."

The author worships these so-called "famous sayings" so decisively that I initially suspected it was an old manuscript written in 1925 or 1926. I hurriedly checked the date, but it was indeed written on "September 23, 1932."

But having quoted "great men" and relied on "famous sayings," one must complete the task. I spent the whole day reading it. As I closed the book and wanted to sleep, I suddenly understood. I took Zhao Jingshen's A Short History of Chinese Literature, Zheng Zhenduo's An Outline of Literature, and Karl Radek's History of the Chinese Revolutionary Movement and compared them carefully. I discovered that the method of Mr. Yu's "materialist research" in this "decent" work is: History of the Chinese Revolutionary Movement + A Short History of Chinese Literature + An Outline of Literature + Controversy on Chinese Social History (Antique Junk Stall), volumes one and two. A World Literary History in "Silhouette Collection."

If you don't believe me, Radek, though a "devil," has no way to testify. Zheng Zhenduo is far away in Beijing and cannot be consulted. But Zhao Jingshen, old brother, if you have read this "decent" work, you will surely understand.

Although Zheng Zhenduo's An Outline of Literature is crude and has many omissions, one cannot help but admire his perseverance. Mr. Yu's great work is clipped and copied from everywhere, but one cannot help but admire his boldness.

Such a brilliant hand, how can it not be praised? I am not talented, but I must express it and attach it to that "Collection of Praises"!

Creative Novel

Ordinary Affairs (12)

— 𣽃 Guo Sun

Zhi Guang passed the old site of the Dananmen city gate. Looking west, he could already see the iron sign of the Changxing Construction Company erected high on the roof of the building. Although the "Nian'an" electrical advertising on the sign did not appear very bright during the day, the tall iron frame could already show the prosperity of Changxing. Walking a little further, he saw several workers standing outside the factory gate, looking up at the sky idly.

The factory was so silent that it almost made one suspect it was a Sunday morning. Materials lay in their respective places, and tools were arranged in their respective positions. The only things moving were three or five workers living in the factory, going back and forth to get water from the large tap. The "pu si deng deng" sound of Zhi Guang's bicycle made them look up. Zhi Guang nodded and smiled at them before turning a corner and getting off his bike in front of the office.

Three or five minutes later, several representatives of the workers had received the message and came to talk to Zhi Guang:

"Mr. Zhang," said a representative surnamed Lin, "the matter of us helping Zhabei last night still depends on you and Mr. Yao to smooth things over."

"That's right," Zhi Guang said, "I came specifically for this matter. But the factory has helped Zhabei several times before."

"We know that very well. But as we see the situation now, Zhabei's need for help is getting more urgent by the day."

"What kind of supplies are needed?" asked a representative surnamed Qiu. "We hear the usage is getting greater every day. We hear the supplies the factory had stored up are being used up faster and faster. The people from the factory who went there all said that…" Hearing this, Zhi Guang's myopic eyes, hidden under thick eyebrows, almost wrinkled until there were no gaps. Only his mouth, like two half-opened lotus leaves, and the row of white jade-like teeth inside could express Zhi Guang's intelligence. He asked:

"How many people from the factory went?"

"We don't have an exact number," Mr. Lin said, "but more people from our masonry group went than from the carpentry group."

"There were quite a few from the carpentry group too," Mr. Qiu interrupted, "except for those doing fine woodworking."

Then they took turns telling Zhi Guang many names and the many things these names had seen or done: heroic, passionate, heartbroken, joyful, making others unable to disbelieve, and unwilling to disbelieve, yet they had to listen quietly. Zhi Guang started by listening quietly, but later the power of these reports made him think of two stories he had almost witnessed when he was working in France,

At that time, the European War had not yet stopped. He was working in an iron factory in southern France. There were more than a hundred Chinese workers in this factory, and in another nearby factory, there were more than two hundred African black people doing unloading and carrying work. One day, probably on a major commemorative holiday when everyone was resting, some of these two different colored workers were playing in the wild. They misunderstood each other and clashed, and in less than half a day, it turned into a large-scale brawl. Because of their small number, the Chinese workers saw that they could not hold on. They were being forced by the black people to the edge of a large lake, seemingly in a backwater situation. Suddenly, eight or ninety more Chinese workers came from the side and attacked the black people fiercely. With great difficulty, those Chinese workers on the edge of the lake escaped danger. Later, they thanked the other group, and only then did they learn that the reinforcements were all Annamese workers. Two or three days later, the local judicial official investigated the three kinds of people who were injured in this brawl from all sides and determined that they were all the main culprits who caused the trouble, and summoned them to court… When the judge questioned the Annamese workers, he particularly rebuked them for not minding their own business, and said that they should be severely punished. The Annamese workers first pointed to the faces of the Chinese workers in court, then pointed to their own faces, and said to the judge: "These are all the same, even if you increase the punishment, we will not regret it!" Later, they pointed to the faces of those black people, and shook their hands towards their own faces, saying: "These are not the same!" … At that time, the people who knew about this matter regarded it as a matter worth studying.
